[?2004h]0;vagrant@ubuntu-jammy: /vagrant[01;32mvagrant@ubuntu-jammy[00m:[01;34m/vagrant[00m$ man cal
[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=CAL(1)                                                    BSD General Commands Manual                                                    CAL(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
     [1mcal[0m, [1mncal[0m ‚Äî displays a calendar and the date of Easter[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
     [1mcal[0m [[1m-3hjy[0m] [[1m-A[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-B[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[[4mmonth[24m] [4myear[24m][m
     [1mcal[0m [[1m-3hj[0m] [[1m-A[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-B[0m [4mnumber[24m] [1m-m[0m [4mmonth[24m [[4myear[24m][m
     [1mncal[0m [[1m-3bhjJpwySM[0m] [[1m-A[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-B[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-W[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-s[0m [4mcountry_code[24m] [[[4mmonth[24m] [4myear[24m][m
     [1mncal[0m [[1m-Jeo[0m] [[1m-A[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[1m-B[0m [4mnumber[24m] [[4myear[24m][m
     [1mncal[0m [[1m-CN[0m] [[1m-H[0m [4myyyy-mm-dd[24m] [[1m-d[0m [4myyyy-mm[24m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
     The [1mcal[0m utility displays a simple calendar in traditional format and [1mncal[0m offers an alternative layout, more options and the date of[m
     Easter.  The new format is a little cramped but it makes a year fit on a 25x80 terminal.  If arguments are not specified, the current[m
     month is displayed.[m
[m
     The options are as follows:[m
[m
     [1m-h[0m      Turns off highlighting of today.[m
[m
     [1m-J[0m      Display Julian Calendar, if combined with the [1m-o[0m option, display date of Orthodox Easter according to the Julian Calendar.[m
[m
     [1m-e[0m      Display date of Easter (for western churches).[m
[m
     [1m-j[0m      Display Julian days (days one-based, numbered from January 1).[m
[m
     [1m-m[0m [4mmonth[24m[m
             Display the specified [4mmonth[24m.  If [4mmonth[24m is specified as a decimal number, appending ‚Äòf‚Äô or ‚Äòp‚Äô displays the same month of the fol‚Äê[m
             lowing or previous year respectively.[m
[m
     [1m-o[0m      Display date of Orthodox Easter (Greek and Russian Orthodox Churches).[m
[m
     [1m-p[0m      Print the country codes and switching days from Julian to Gregorian Calendar as they are assumed by [1mncal[0m.  The country code as de‚Äê[m
             termined from the local environment is marked with an asterisk.[m
[m
     [1m-s[0m [4mcountry_code[24m[m
             Assume the switch from Julian to Gregorian Calendar at the date associated with the [4mcountry_code[24m.  If not specified, [1mncal[0m tries to[m
             guess the switch date from the local environment or falls back to September 2, 1752.  This was when Great Britain and her colonies[m
             switched to the Gregorian Calendar.[m
[m
     [1m-w[0m      Print the number of the week below each week column.[m
[m
     [1m-y[0m      Display a calendar for the specified year. This option is implied when a year but no month are specified on the command line.[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[K[7m Manual page cal(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[K[7m Manual page cal(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[K[7m Manual page cal(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-3[0m      Display the previous, current and next month surrounding today.[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-1[0m      Display only the current month. This is the default.[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K     [1m-A[0m [4mnumber[24m[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             Months to add after. The specified number of months is added to the end of the display. This is in addition to any date range se‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             lected by the [1m-y[0m, [1m-3[0m, or [1m-1[0m options. For example, ‚Äúcal -y -B2 -A2‚Äù shows everything from November of the previous year to February[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             of the following year. Negative numbers are allowed, in which case the specified number of months is subtracted. For example, ‚Äúcal[m
[7m Manual page cal(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K             -y -B-6‚Äù shows July to December. And ‚Äúcal -A11‚Äù simply shows the next 12 months.[m

[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=WC(1)                                                            User Commands                                                            WC(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       wc - print newline, word, and byte counts for each file[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mwc[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
       [1mwc[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--files0-from=F[24m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Print  newline,  word,  and byte counts for each FILE, and a total line if more than one FILE is specified.  A word is a non-zero-length[m
       sequence of characters delimited by white space.[m
[m
       With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.[m
[m
       The options below may be used to select which counts are printed, always in the following order: newline, word, character, byte, maximum[m
       line length.[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m, [1m--bytes[0m[m
              print the byte counts[m
[m
       [1m-m[0m, [1m--chars[0m[m
              print the character counts[m
[m
       [1m-l[0m, [1m--lines[0m[m
              print the newline counts[m
[m
       [1m--files0-from[0m=[4mF[24m[m
              read input from the files specified by NUL-terminated names in file F; If F is - then read names from standard input[m
[m
       [1m-L[0m, [1m--max-line-length[0m[m
              print the maximum display width[m
[m
       [1m-w[0m, [1m--words[0m[m
              print the word counts[m
[m
       [1m--help[0m display this help and exit[m
[m
       [1m--version[0m[m
              output version information and exit[m
[m
[1mAUTHOR[0m[m
       Written by Paul Rubin and David MacKenzie.[m
[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       ls - list directory contents[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mls[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       List  information  about  the  FILEs (the current directory by default).  Sort entries alphabetically if none of [1m-cftuvSUX[0m nor [1m--sort[0m is[m
       specified.[m
[m
       Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.[m
[m
       [1m-a[0m, [1m--all[0m[m
              do not ignore entries starting with .[m
[m
       [1m-A[0m, [1m--almost-all[0m[m
              do not list implied . and ..[m
[m
       [1m--author[0m[m
              with [1m-l[0m, print the author of each file[m
[m
       [1m-b[0m, [1m--escape[0m[m
              print C-style escapes for nongraphic characters[m
[m
       [1m--block-size[0m=[4mSIZE[24m[m
              with [1m-l[0m, scale sizes by SIZE when printing them; e.g., '--block-size=M'; see SIZE format below[m
[m
       [1m-B[0m, [1m--ignore-backups[0m[m
              do not list implied entries ending with ~[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m     with [1m-lt[0m: sort by, and show, ctime (time of last modification of file status information); with [1m-l[0m: show ctime and sort by  name;[m
              otherwise: sort by ctime, newest first[m
[m
       [1m-C[0m     list entries by columns[m
[m
       [1m--color[0m[=[4mWHEN[24m][m
              colorize the output; WHEN can be 'always' (default if omitted), 'auto', or 'never'; more info below[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--directory[0m[m
              list directories themselves, not their contents[m
[m
       [1m-D[0m, [1m--dired[0m[m

[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=SORT(1)                                                          User Commands                                                          SORT(1)[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       sort - sort lines of text files[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1msort[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
       [1msort[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--files0-from=F[24m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Write sorted concatenation of all FILE(s) to standard output.[m
[m
       With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.[m
[m
       Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.  Ordering options:[m
[m
       [1m-b[0m, [1m--ignore-leading-blanks[0m[m
              ignore leading blanks[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--dictionary-order[0m[m
              consider only blanks and alphanumeric characters[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--ignore-case[0m[m
              fold lower case to upper case characters[m
[m
       [1m-g[0m, [1m--general-numeric-sort[0m[m
              compare according to general numerical value[m
[m
       [1m-i[0m, [1m--ignore-nonprinting[0m[m
              consider only printable characters[m
[m
       [1m-M[0m, [1m--month-sort[0m[m
              compare (unknown) < 'JAN' < ... < 'DEC'[m
[m
       [1m-h[0m, [1m--human-numeric-sort[0m[m
              compare human readable numbers (e.g., 2K 1G)[m
[m
       [1m-n[0m, [1m--numeric-sort[0m[m
              compare according to string numerical value[m
[m
       [1m-R[0m, [1m--random-sort[0m[m
              shuffle, but group identical keys.  See shuf(1)[m
[m
       [1m--random-source[0m=[4mFILE[24m[m

These are common Git commands used in various situations:

start a working area (see also: git help tutorial)
   clone     Clone a repository into a new directory
   init      Create an empty Git repository or reinitialize an existing one

work on the current change (see also: git help everyday)
   add       Add file contents to the index
   mv        Move or rename a file, a directory, or a symlink
   restore   Restore working tree files
   rm        Remove files from the working tree and from the index

examine the history and state (see also: git help revisions)
   bisect    Use binary search to find the commit that introduced a bug
   diff      Show changes between commits, commit and working tree, etc
   grep      Print lines matching a pattern
   log       Show commit logs
   show      Show various types of objects
   status    Show the working tree status

grow, mark and tweak your common history
   branch    List, create, or delete branches
   commit    Record changes to the repository
   merge     Join two or more development histories together
   rebase    Reapply commits on top of another base tip
   reset     Reset current HEAD to the specified state
   switch    Switch branches
   tag       Create, list, delete or verify a tag object signed with GPG

collaborate (see also: git help workflows)
   fetch     Download objects and refs from another repository
   pull      Fetch from and integrate with another repository or a local branch
   push      Update remote refs along with associated objects

'git help -a' and 'git help -g' list available subcommands and some
concept guides. See 'git help <command>' or 'git help <concept>'
to read about a specific subcommand or concept.
